---
  description: Wraps a 1d sequence of panels into 2d and then convert them with ggplotly.
  function: facet_wrap
  permalink: /ggplot2/Facetting/facet_wrap/
  layout: base
  language: ggplot2
  name: facet_wrap
  reference: https://ggplot2.tidyverse.org/reference/
---


# Default plot

<pre class="mcode">
p <- ggplot(mpg, aes(displ, hwy)) + geom_point()
p <-  p + facet_wrap(vars(class))

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

Use the `labeller` option to control how labels are printed:


<pre class="mcode">
p <-    
 ggplot(mpg, aes(displ, hwy)) +
  geom_point() +
  facet_wrap(vars(cyl, drv), labeller = "label_both")
  
plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

# Order of facets

To change the order in which the panels appear, change the levels of the underlying factor.



<pre class="mcode">
mpg$class2 <- reorder(mpg$class, mpg$displ)
p <-  ggplot(mpg, aes(displ, hwy)) +
p <-    geom_point() +
p <-    facet_wrap(vars(class2))

plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

By default, the same scales are used for all panels. You can allow scales to vary across the panels with the `scales` argument.

Free scales make it easier to see patterns within each panel, but harder to compare across panels.


<pre class="mcode">
p <-    
 ggplot(mpg, aes(displ, hwy)) +
  geom_point() +
  facet_wrap(vars(class), scales = "free")
  
plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

To repeat the same data in every panel, simply construct a data frame that does not contain the faceting variable.


<pre class="mcode">
p <-    
 ggplot(mpg, aes(displ, hwy)) +
  geom_point(data = transform(mpg, class = NULL), colour = "grey85") +
  geom_point() +
  facet_wrap(vars(class))
  
plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>

Use `strip.position` to display the facet labels at the side of your choice. Setting it to `bottom` makes it act as a subtitle for the axis.

This is typically used with free scales and a theme without boxes around strip labels.



<pre class="mcode">
p <-    
 ggplot(economics_long, aes(date, value)) +
  geom_line() +
  facet_wrap(vars(variable), scales = "free_y", nrow = 2, strip.position = "top") +
  theme(strip.background = element_blank(), strip.placement = "outside")
  
plotly::ggplotly(p)
</pre>
